scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Total</div></th><td>$9.183&#160;billion<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Per capita</div></th><td>$707<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(2012)</span></th><td>33.7<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><br /><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:orange">medium</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">HDI</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(2017)</span></th><td><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" traffic">Driving side</a></th><td>right</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Guinea" title="Telephone numbers in Guinea">Calling code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/%2B224" class="mw-redirect" title="+224">+224</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:GN" title="ISO 3166-2:GN">GN</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.gn" title=".gn">.gn</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Guinea</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Guinea.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/En-us-Guinea.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Guinea.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Guinea</b> (French: <i lang="fr">République de Guinée</i>), is a west-coastal country in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. Formerly known as <a href="/wiki/French_Guinea" title="French Guinea">French Guinea</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Guinée française</i>), the modern country is sometimes referred to as <b>Guinea-Conakry</b> in order to distinguish it from other countries with "Guinea" in the name and the <a href="/wiki/Guinea_(region)" title="Guinea (region)">eponymous region</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uiowa1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uiowa1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Guinea has a population of 12.4 million and an area of 245,860 square kilometres (94,927&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-guinea_stats_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guinea_stats-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Guinea is a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> with a president who is directly elected by the people; this position is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>.  The unicameral <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Guinea)" title="National Assembly (Guinea)">Guinean National Assembly</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_body" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative body">legislative body</a> of the country, and its members are also directly elected by the people.  The judicial branch is led by the Guinea Supreme Court, the highest and final court of appeal in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The country is named after the <a href="/wiki/Guinea_(region)" title="Guinea (region)">Guinea region</a>. Guinea is a traditional name for the region of Africa that lies along the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a>. It stretches north through the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">forested tropical regions</a> and ends at the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a>. The English term Guinea comes directly from the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> word <i>Guiné</i>, which emerged in the mid-15th century to refer to the lands inhabited by the <i>Guineus</i>, a generic term for the black African peoples south of the <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal River</a>, in contrast to the "<a href="/wiki/Tawny_(color)" title="Tawny (color)">tawny</a>" Zenaga Berbers above it, whom they called <i>Azenegues</i> or <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>.
</p><p>Guinea is a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> country, with <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> representing 85 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uiowa1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uiowa1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Guinea's people belong to twenty-four <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Guinea" title="Demographics of Guinea">ethnic groups</a>.  French, the official language of Guinea, is the main language of communication in schools, in government administration, and the media, but more than twenty-four indigenous languages are also spoken.
</p><p>Guinea's economy is largely dependent on agriculture and <a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">mineral</a> production.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It is the world's second largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>, and has rich deposits of <a href="/wiki/Diamonds" class="mw-redirect" title="Diamonds">diamonds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guineaconakrysupport.com_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guineaconakrysupport.com-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The country was at the core of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Ebola_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Ebola outbreak">2014 Ebola outbreak</a>. <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Guinea" title="Human rights in Guinea">Human rights in Guinea</a> remain a controversial issue. In 2011 the United States government claimed that <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> by security forces, and abuse of women and children (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>) were ongoing abuses of human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-State_2011_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_2011-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Guinea%22">"Guinea"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Guinea%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Guinea%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Guinea%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Guinea%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Guinea%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guinea" title="History of Guinea">History of Guinea</a></div>
<p>The land that is now Guinea belonged to a series of African empires until France colonized it in the 1890s, and made it part of <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a>. Guinea declared its independence from France on 2 October 1958. From independence until the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_presidential_election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean presidential election, 2010">presidential election</a> of 2010, Guinea was governed by a number of <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocratic</a> rulers.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the origin of the name "Guinea" see <a href="/wiki/Guinea_(region)#Etymology" title="Guinea (region)">Guinea (region) §&#160;Etymology</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_African_empires_and_Kingdoms_in_Guinea">West African empires and Kingdoms in Guinea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: West African empires and Kingdoms in Guinea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Imamate_of_Futa_Jallon" title="Imamate of Futa Jallon">Imamate of Futa Jallon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wassoulou_Empire" title="Wassoulou Empire">Wassoulou Empire</a></div>
<p>What is now Guinea was on the fringes of the major <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> empires. The earliest, the <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana Empire</a>, grew on trade but ultimately fell after repeated incursions of the <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a>. It was in this period that Islam first arrived in the region by way of North African traders.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sosso" class="mw-redirect" title="Sosso">Sosso</a> kingdom (12th to 13th centuries) briefly flourished in the resulting void but the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> came to prominence when <a href="/wiki/Sundiata_Keita" title="Sundiata Keita">Soundiata Kéïta</a> defeated the Sosso ruler <a href="/wiki/Soumaoro_Kant%C3%A9" title="Soumaoro Kanté">Soumangourou Kanté</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kirina" title="Battle of Kirina">Battle of Kirina</a> in c. 1235. The Mali Empire was ruled by <a href="/wiki/Mansa_(title)" title="Mansa (title)">Mansa</a> (Emperors), the most famous being <a href="/wiki/Musa_I_of_Mali" title="Musa I of Mali">Kankou Moussa</a>, who made a famous <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">hajj</a> to Mecca in 1324. Shortly after his reign the Mali Empire began to decline and was ultimately supplanted by its <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassal</a> states in the 15th century.
</p><p>The most successful of these was the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a>, which expanded its power from about 1460 and eventually surpassed the Mali Empire in both territory and wealth. It continued to prosper until a civil war over succession followed the death of <a href="/wiki/Askia_Daoud" title="Askia Daoud">Askia Daoud</a> in 1582. The weakened empire fell to invaders from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tondibi" title="Battle of Tondibi">Battle of Tondibi</a> just three years later. The Moroccans proved unable to rule the kingdom effectively, however, and it split into many small kingdoms.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Almamy_Samory_Tour%C3%A9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Almamy_Samory_Tour%C3%A9.jpg/220px-Almamy_Samory_Tour%C3%A9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Almamy_Samory_Tour%C3%A9.jpg/330px-Almamy_Samory_Tour%C3%A9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/Almamy_Samory_Tour%C3%A9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="457" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Almamy_Samory_Tour%C3%A9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Samori_Toure" class="mw-redirect" title="Samori Toure">Samori Toure</a> was the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Wassoulou_Empire" title="Wassoulou Empire">Wassoulou Empire</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Islamic" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic">Islamic</a> state in present-day Guinea that resisted <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> colonial rule in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> from 1882 until Touré's capture in 1898.</div></div></div>
<p>After the fall of the major West African empires, various kingdoms existed in what is now Guinea. <a href="/wiki/Fulani" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulani">Fulani</a> Muslims migrated to <a href="/wiki/Futa_Jallon" class="mw-redirect" title="Futa Jallon">Futa Jallon</a> in Central Guinea and established an Islamic state from 1735 to 1898 with a written constitution and alternate rulers. The <a href="/wiki/Wassoulou_Empire" title="Wassoulou Empire">Wassoulou or Wassulu empire</a> was a short-lived (1878–1898) empire, led by <a href="/wiki/Samori_Toure" class="mw-redirect" title="Samori Toure">Samori Toure</a> in the predominantly <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Malinké</a> area of what is now upper Guinea and southwestern <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> (Wassoulou). It moved to <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> before being conquered by the French.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> came to the coastal region of Guinea with European traders in the 16th century. Slaves were exported to work elsewhere in the <a href="/wiki/Triangular_trade" title="Triangular trade">triangular trade</a>.
</p><p>Guinea's colonial period began with French military penetration into the area in the mid-19th century. French domination was assured by the defeat in 1898 of the armies of <a href="/wiki/Samori_Tour%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Samori Touré">Samori Touré</a>, Mansa (or Emperor) of the <a href="/wiki/Ouassoulou" class="mw-redirect" title="Ouassoulou">Ouassoulou</a> state and leader of Malinké descent, which gave France control of what today is Guinea and adjacent areas.
</p><p>France negotiated Guinea's present boundaries in the late 19th and early 20th centuries with the British for <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, the Portuguese for their Guinea colony (now <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>. Under the French, the country formed the <a href="/wiki/French_Guinea" title="French Guinea">Territory of Guinea</a> within <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a>, administered by a governor general resident in <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>. Lieutenant governors administered the individual colonies, including Guinea.
</p>
<h3><span id="Independence_and_post-colonial_rule_.281958.E2.80.932008.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_post-colonial_rule_(1958–2008)">Independence and post-colonial rule (1958–2008)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Independence and post-colonial rule (1958–2008)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1958, the <a href="/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic" title="French Fourth Republic">French Fourth Republic</a> collapsed due to political instability and its failures in dealing with its colonies, especially <a href="/wiki/Indochina" class="mw-redirect" title="Indochina">Indochina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>. The founding of a <a href="/wiki/French_Fifth_Republic" title="French Fifth Republic">Fifth Republic</a> was supported by the French people, while French President <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> made it clear on 8 August 1958 that France's colonies were to be given a stark choice between more <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous entity">autonomy</a> in a new <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a> or immediate independence in the referendum to be held on 28 September 1958. The other colonies chose the former but Guinea—under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9" title="Ahmed Sékou Touré">Ahmed Sékou Touré</a> whose <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Guinea-African_Democratic_Rally" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Party of Guinea-African Democratic Rally">Democratic Party of Guinea-African Democratic Rally</a> (PDG) had won 56 of 60 seats in 1957 territorial elections — voted overwhelmingly for independence. The French withdrew quickly, and on 2 October 1958, Guinea proclaimed itself a sovereign and independent republic, with Sékou Touré as president.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_%283%29.jpg/220px-Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_%283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_%283%29.jpg/330px-Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_%283%29.jpg/440px-Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1732" data-file-height="1126" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9_na_obisku_v_Ljubljani_1961_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_S%C3%A9kou_Tour%C3%A9" title="Ahmed Sékou Touré">Ahmed Sékou Touré</a> was supported by the Communist bloc states and in 1961 visited <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>France's withdrawal resulted in punitive economic reprisals, including the end of all French aid and investment. Guinea subsequently quickly aligned itself with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and adopted <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> policies. This alliance was short-lived, however, as Guinea moved towards a Chinese model of socialism. Despite this, however, the country continued to receive aid and investment from <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> countries such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.
</p><p>By 1960, Touré had declared the PDG the country's only legal political party and for the next 24 years, the government and the PDG were one.  Touré was reelected unopposed to four seven-year terms as president, and every five years voters were presented with a single list of PDG candidates for the National Assembly. Advocating a hybrid <a href="/wiki/African_Socialism" class="mw-redirect" title="African Socialism">African Socialism</a> domestically and <a href="/wiki/Pan-Africanism" title="Pan-Africanism">Pan-Africanism</a> abroad, Touré quickly became a polarising leader, and his government became intolerant of dissent, imprisoning thousands and stifling the press.
</p><p>Throughout the 1960s the Guinean government nationalised land, removed French-appointed and traditional chiefs from power, and had strained ties with the French government and French companies. Touré's government relied on the Soviet Union and China for infrastructure aid and development but much of this was used for political and not economic purposes (such as the building of large stadiums to hold political rallies). Meanwhile, the country's roads, railways and other infrastructure languished and the economy stagnated.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:22novemberdetail.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/22novemberdetail.JPG/220px-22novemberdetail.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="362" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/22novemberdetail.JPG/330px-22novemberdetail.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/22novemberdetail.JPG/440px-22novemberdetail.JPG 2x" data-file-width="455" data-file-height="749" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:22novemberdetail.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument to commemorate the 1970 military victory over the Portuguese raid. The only objective not accomplished by the Portuguese raid was the capture of Ahmed Sékou Touré.</div></div></div>
<p>On 22 November 1970, Portuguese forces from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a> staged <a href="/wiki/Operation_Green_Sea" title="Operation Green Sea">Operation Green Sea</a>, a raid on Conakry by several hundred exiled Guinean opposition forces. Among their goals, the Portuguese military wanted to kill or capture Sekou Toure due his support of the <a href="/wiki/PAIGC" class="mw-redirect" title="PAIGC">PAIGC</a>, an independence movement and rebel group that carried out attacks inside Portuguese Guinea from their bases in Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> After fierce fighting, the Portuguese-backed forces retreated, having freed several dozen Portuguese prisoners of war that were being held by the PAIGC in Conakry but without having ousted Touré. In the years after the raid, massive purges were carried out by the Touré government and at least 50,000 people (1% of Guinea's entire population) were killed. Countless others were imprisoned, faced torture, or, often in the case of foreigners, were forced to leave the country (sometimes after having had their Guinean spouse arrested and their children placed into state custody).
</p><p>A declining economy, mass killings, a stifling political atmosphere, and a ban on all private economic transactions led in 1977 to the "<a href="/wiki/Guinean_Market_Women%27s_Revolt" title="Guinean Market Women&#39;s Revolt">Market Women's Revolt</a>", anti-government riots that were started by women working in Conakry's <a href="/wiki/March%C3%A9_Madina_(Conakry)" title="Marché Madina (Conakry)">Madina Market</a>. This caused Touré to make major reforms. Touré vacillated from supporting the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> to supporting the United States. The late 1970s and early 1980s saw some economic reforms but Touré's centralized control of the state remained. Even the relationship with France improved; after the election of <a href="/wiki/Val%C3%A9ry_Giscard_d%27Estaing" title="Valéry Giscard d&#39;Estaing">Valéry Giscard d'Estaing</a> as French president, trade increased and the two countries exchanged diplomatic visits.
</p><p>Sékou Touré died on 26 March 1984 after a heart operation in the United States, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_Government_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of Government of Guinea">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Louis_Lansana_Beavogui" title="Louis Lansana Beavogui">Louis Lansana Beavogui</a>, who was to serve as interim president pending new elections. The PDG was due to elect a new leader on 3 April 1984. Under the constitution, that person would have been the only candidate for president. However, hours before that meeting, Colonels <a href="/wiki/Lansana_Cont%C3%A9" title="Lansana Conté">Lansana Conté</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diarra_Traor%C3%A9" title="Diarra Traoré">Diarra Traoré</a> seized power in a bloodless <a href="/wiki/Coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Coup">coup</a>. Conté assumed the role of president, with Traoré serving as prime minister until December.
</p><p>Conté immediately denounced the previous regime's record on <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>, released 250 political prisoners and encouraged approximately 200,000 more to return from exile. He also made explicit the turn away from socialism. This did little to alleviate poverty and the country showed no immediate signs of moving towards <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>.
</p><p>In 1992, Conté announced a return to civilian rule, with a presidential poll in 1993 followed by elections to parliament in 1995 (in which his party—the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Unity_and_Progress" class="mw-redirect" title="Party of Unity and Progress">Party of Unity and Progress</a>—won 71 of 114 seats.) Despite his stated commitment to democracy, Conté's grip on power remained tight. In September 2001, the opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Condé">Alpha Condé</a> was imprisoned for endangering state security, though he was pardoned 8 months later. He subsequently spent a period of exile in France.
</p><p>In 2001, Conté organized and won a referendum to lengthen the presidential term and in 2003 begun his third term after elections were boycotted by the opposition. In January 2005, Conté survived a suspected assassination attempt while making a rare public appearance in the capital <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>. His opponents claimed that he was a "tired dictator"<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> whose departure was inevitable, whereas his supporters believed that he was winning a battle with dissidents. Guinea still faces very real problems and according to <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy" title="Foreign Policy">Foreign Policy</a> is in danger of becoming a <a href="/wiki/Failed_state" title="Failed state">failed state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2000, Guinea became embroiled in the instability which had long blighted the rest of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> as rebels crossed the borders with <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> and it seemed for a time that the country was headed for <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">civil war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Conté blamed neighbouring leaders for coveting Guinea's natural resources, though these claims were strenuously denied.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, Guinea agreed to plans with her neighbours to tackle the insurgents. In 2007, there were <a href="/wiki/2007_Guinean_general_strike" title="2007 Guinean general strike">large protests</a> against the government, resulting in the appointment of a new prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Conté remained in power until his death on 23 December 2008<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and several hours following his death, <a href="/wiki/Moussa_Dadis_Camara" title="Moussa Dadis Camara">Moussa Dadis Camara</a> seized control in a <a href="/wiki/2008_Guinean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2008 Guinean coup d&#39;état">coup</a>, declaring himself head of a <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">military junta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Protests against the coup became violent and 157 people were killed when, on 28 September 2009, the junta ordered its soldiers to attack people who had gathered to protest against Camara's attempt to become president.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The soldiers went on a rampage of rape, mutilation, and murder which caused many foreign governments to withdraw their support for the new regime.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 December 2009, an aide shot Camara during a dispute over the rampage in September. Camara went to Morocco for medical care.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Vice-President (and defense minister) <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9kouba_Konat%C3%A9" title="Sékouba Konaté">Sékouba Konaté</a> flew back from <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> to run the country in Camara's absence.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> After meeting in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a> on 13 and 14 January 2010, Camara, Konaté and <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a>, President of <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>, produced a formal statement of twelve principles promising a return of Guinea to civilian rule within six months.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The presidential election was held on 27 June,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-transitional_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transitional-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> with a second election held on 7 November due to allegations of electoral fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Voter turnout was high, and the elections went relatively smoothly.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Condé">Alpha Condé</a>, leader of the opposition party <a href="/wiki/Rally_of_the_Guinean_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Rally of the Guinean People">Rally of the Guinean People</a> (RGP), won the election promising to reform the security sector and review mining contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late February 2013, <a href="/wiki/2013_Guinea_Violence" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Guinea Violence">political violence erupted in Guinea</a> after protesters took to the streets to voice their concerns over the transparency of the upcoming May 2013 elections. The demonstrations were fueled by the opposition coalition's decision to step down from the electoral process in protest at the lack of transparency in the preparations for elections.<sup id="cite_ref-Rone_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rone-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Nine people were killed during the protests, and around 220 were injured. Many of the deaths and injuries were caused by security forces using live ammunition on protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rtwo_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rtwo-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The political violence also led to inter-ethnic clashes between the <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malinke" class="mw-redirect" title="Malinke">Malinke</a>, the base of support for President Condé. The former mainly supported the opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 March 2013, the opposition party backed out of the negotiations with the government over the upcoming 12 May election. The opposition said that the government had not respected them, and had not kept any promises they agreed to.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 March 2014, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> said that <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Guinea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Health (Guinea)">Guinea's Ministry of Health</a> had reported <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_Guinea" title="Ebola virus epidemic in Guinea">an outbreak</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_disease" title="Ebola virus disease">Ebola virus disease</a> in Guinea. This initial outbreak had a total of 86 cases, including 59 deaths. By 28 May, there were 281 cases, with 186 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It is believed that the first case was Emile Ouamouno, a 2-year-old boy who lived in the village of <a href="/wiki/Meliandou" title="Meliandou">Meliandou</a>. He fell ill on 2 December 2013 and died on 6 December.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 18 September 2014, eight members of an Ebola education health care team <a href="/wiki/Womey_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Womey Massacre">were murdered</a> by villagers in the town of <a href="/wiki/Womey" title="Womey">Womey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> As of 1 November 2015, there have been 3,810 cases and 2,536 deaths in Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guinea" title="Politics of Guinea">Politics of Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg/220px-Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="321" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg/330px-Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg/440px-Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3592" data-file-height="5240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alpha_Conde_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Condé">Alpha Condé</a>, the current President of Guinea</div></div></div>
<p>The country is a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. The president is directly elected by the people and is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. The unicameral National Assembly is the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_body" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative body">legislative body</a> of the country, and its members are directly elected by the people. The judicial branch is led by the Guinea Supreme Court, the highest and final court of appeal in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Guinea is a member of many international organizations including the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agency_for_the_French-Speaking_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Agency for the French-Speaking Community">Agency for the French-Speaking Community</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Development_Bank" title="Islamic Development Bank">Islamic Development Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>President <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Condé">Alpha Condé</a> derives support from Guinea's second-largest ethnic group, the <a href="/wiki/Malinke" class="mw-redirect" title="Malinke">Malinke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea_2013_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea_2013-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Guinea's opposition is backed by the <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a> ethnic group,<sup id="cite_ref-Fula_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fula-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> who account for around 40 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea_2013_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea_2013-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Executive branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Guinea">president of Guinea</a> is normally elected by popular vote for a five-year term; the winning candidate must receive a majority of the votes cast to be elected president. The president governs Guinea, assisted by a <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council">council</a> of 25 civilian <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">ministers</a> appointed by him. The government administers the country through eight regions, 33 <a href="/wiki/Prefecture" title="Prefecture">prefectures</a>, over 100 <a href="/wiki/Subprefecture" title="Subprefecture">subprefectures</a>, and many districts (known as <a href="/wiki/Commune_(subnational_entity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Commune (subnational entity)">communes</a> in <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> and other large cities and villages or "quartiers" in the interior). District-level leaders are elected; the president appoints officials to all other levels of the highly centralized administration.
</p><p>Since the 2010 presidential elections, the head of state has been <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Condé">Alpha Condé</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Legislative branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Guinea">National Assembly of Guinea</a>, the country's legislative body, did not meet from 2008 to 2013 when it was dissolved after the military coup in December. <a href="/wiki/Guinean_legislative_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean legislative election, 2013">Elections</a> have been postponed many times since 2007. In April 2012, President Condé postponed the elections indefinitely, citing the need to ensure that they were "transparent and democratic".<sup id="cite_ref-RNW_Africa_Desk_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RNW_Africa_Desk-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Guinean_legislative_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean legislative election, 2013">2013 Guinean legislative election</a> were held on 24 September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Condé">Alpha Condé</a>'s party, the <a href="/wiki/Rally_of_the_Guinean_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Rally of the Guinean People">Rally of the Guinean People</a> (RPG), won a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> of seats in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Guinea">National Assembly of Guinea</a>, with 53 out of 114 seats. The opposition parties won a total of 53 seats, and opposition leaders denounced the official results as fraudulent.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Guinea" title="Foreign relations of Guinea">Foreign relations of Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_(2017-09-28)_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_%282017-09-28%29_2.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_%282017-09-28%29_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_%282017-09-28%29_2.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_%282017-09-28%29_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_%282017-09-28%29_2.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_%282017-09-28%29_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Alpha_Cond%C3%A9_(2017-09-28)_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Condé">Alpha Condé</a> with Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> on 28 September 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Guinea's foreign relations, including those with its <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> neighbors, have improved steadily since 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Guinea">Military of Guinea</a></div>
<p>Guinea's armed forces are divided into five branches – army, navy, air force, the paramilitary National <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">Gendarmerie</a> and the Republican Guard – whose chiefs report to the Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff, who is subordinate to the Minister of Defense. In addition, regime security forces include the National Police Force (Sûreté National). The Gendarmerie, responsible for internal security, has a strength of several thousand.
</p><p>The army, with about 15,000 personnel, is by far the largest branch of the armed forces.  It is mainly responsible for protecting the state borders, the security of administered territories, and defending Guinea's national interests. Air force personnel total about 700. The force's equipment includes several Russian-supplied fighter planes and transports. The navy has about 900 personnel and operates several small <a href="/wiki/Patrol_craft" class="mw-redirect" title="Patrol craft">patrol craft</a> and barges.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Un-guinea.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Un-guinea.png/650px-Un-guinea.png" decoding="async" width="650" height="498" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Un-guinea.png/975px-Un-guinea.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Un-guinea.png/1300px-Un-guinea.png 2x" data-file-width="3092" data-file-height="2367" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Un-guinea.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Guinea" title="List of cities in Guinea">Guinea's cities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of Guinea">administrative divisions</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg/300px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg/450px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg/600px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1321" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_GIN_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Guinea map of Köppen climate classification</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Guinea" title="Geography of Guinea">Geography of Guinea</a></div>
<p>Guinea shares a border with <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> on the north, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> on the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> to the south. The nation forms a crescent as it curves from its southeast region to the north and west, to its northwest border with <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a> and southwestern coast on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. The sources of the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gambia_River" title="Gambia River">Gambia River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal River</a> are all found in the <a href="/wiki/Guinea_Highlands" title="Guinea Highlands">Guinea Highlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At 245,857&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (94,926&#160;sq&#160;mi), Guinea is roughly the size of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. There are 320&#160;km (200&#160;mi) of coastline and a total land border of 3,400&#160;km (2,100&#160;mi). It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/7th_parallel_north" title="7th parallel north">7°</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/7th_meridian_west" title="7th meridian west">7°</a> and <a href="/wiki/15th_meridian_west" title="15th meridian west">15°W</a> (a small area is west of 15°).
</p><p>Guinea is divided into four main regions: <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Guinea" title="Maritime Guinea">Maritime Guinea</a>, also known as Lower Guinea or the Basse-Coté lowlands, populated mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Susu_people" title="Susu people">Susu</a> ethnic group; the cooler, mountainous <a href="/wiki/Fouta_Djallon" title="Fouta Djallon">Fouta Djallon</a> that run roughly north-south through the middle of the country, populated by Fulas, the Sahelian Haute-Guinea to the northeast, populated by <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Malinké</a>, and the forested jungle regions in the southeast, with several ethnic groups. Guinea's mountains are the source for the Niger, the Gambia, and Senegal Rivers, as well as the numerous rivers flowing to the sea on the west side of the range in Sierra Leone and Ivory Coast.
</p><p>The highest point in Guinea is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Nimba" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Nimba">Mount Nimba</a> at 1,752&#160;m (5,748&#160;ft). Although the Guinean and Ivorian sides of the <a href="/wiki/Nimba_Massif" class="mw-redirect" title="Nimba Massif">Nimba Massif</a> are a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Strict_Nature_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Strict Nature Reserve">Strict Nature Reserve</a>, the portion of the so-called Guinean Backbone continues into <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, where it has been mined for decades; the damage is quite evident in the <a href="/wiki/Nz%C3%A9r%C3%A9kor%C3%A9_Region" title="Nzérékoré Region">Nzérékoré Region</a> at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Guinea&amp;params=7_32_17_N_8_29_50_W_region:GN_type:landmark"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">7°32′17″N</span> <span class="longitude">8°29′50″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">7.53806°N 8.49722°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">7.53806; -8.49722</span></span></span></a></span>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_prefectures">Regions and prefectures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Regions and prefectures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of Guinea">Administrative divisions of Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Regions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Guinea_Regions.png/350px-Guinea_Regions.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Guinea_Regions.png 1.5x" data-file-width="386" data-file-height="314" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Regions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Guinea" title="Regions of Guinea">Regions of Guinea</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Republic of Guinea covers 245,857 square kilometres (94,926&#160;sq&#160;mi) of West Africa, about <a href="/wiki/10th_parallel_north" title="10th parallel north">10 degrees north</a> of the equator. Guinea is divided into four natural regions with distinct human, geographic, and climatic characteristics:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Maritime_Guinea" title="Maritime Guinea">Maritime Guinea</a> (<i>La Guinée Maritime</i>) covers 18% of the country.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Middle_Guinea" title="Middle Guinea">Middle Guinea</a> (<i>La Moyenne-Guinée</i>) covers 20% of the country.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Upper_Guinea" title="Upper Guinea">Upper Guinea</a> (<i>La Haute-Guinée</i>) covers 38% of the country.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guin%C3%A9e_foresti%C3%A8re" title="Guinée forestière">Forested Guinea</a> (<i>Guinée forestière</i>) covers 23% of the country, and is both forested and mountainous.</li></ul>
<p>Guinea is divided into eight <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Guinea" title="Regions of Guinea">administrative regions</a> and subdivided into thirty-three <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Guinea" title="Prefectures of Guinea">prefectures</a>. <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> is Guinea's capital, largest city, and economic centre. <a href="/wiki/Nz%C3%A9r%C3%A9kor%C3%A9" title="Nzérékoré">Nzérékoré</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Guin%C3%A9e_foresti%C3%A8re" title="Guinée forestière">Guinée forestière</a> region in Southern Guinea, is the second largest city.
</p><p>Other major cities in the country with a population above 100,000 include <a href="/wiki/Kankan" title="Kankan">Kankan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kindia" title="Kindia">Kindia</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Lab%C3%A9" title="Labé">Labe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A9ck%C3%A9dou" title="Guéckédou">Guéckédou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bok%C3%A9" title="Boké">Boke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamou" title="Mamou">Mamou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kissidougou" title="Kissidougou">Kissidougou</a>.
</p>
<ul><li>The capital <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> with a population of 1,667,864 ranks as a special zone.</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Guinea" title="Wildlife of Guinea">Wildlife of Guinea</a></div>
<p>The wildlife of Guinea is very diverse due to the wide variety of different habitats. The southern part of the country lies within <a href="/wiki/Guinean_Forests_of_West_Africa" title="Guinean Forests of West Africa">Guinean Forests of West Africa</a> <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">Biodiversity Hotspot</a>, while the north-east is characterized by dry savanna woodlands. Unfortunately, declining populations of large animals are restricted to uninhabited distant parts of parks and reserves.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomy">Taxonomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Taxonomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Species found in Guinea include the following:
</p>
<ul><li>Amphibians&#160;: <i><a href="/wiki/Hemisus_guineensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Hemisus guineensis">Hemisus guineensis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Phrynobatrachus_guineensis" title="Phrynobatrachus guineensis">Phrynobatrachus guineensis</a></i></li>
<li>Reptiles&#160;: <i><a href="/wiki/Acanthodactylus" title="Acanthodactylus">Acanthodactylus</a> guineensis</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mochlus" title="Mochlus">Mochlus</a> guineensis</i></li>
<li>Arachnids: <i><a href="/wiki/Malloneta_guineensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Malloneta guineensis">Malloneta guineensis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dictyna" title="Dictyna">Dictyna</a> guineensis</i></li>
<li>Insects&#160;: <i><a href="/wiki/Zorotypus" class="mw-redirect" title="Zorotypus">Zorotypus</a> guineensis</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Euchromia_guineensis" title="Euchromia guineensis">Euchromia guineensis</a></i></li>
<li>Birds: <i><a href="/wiki/Melaniparus_guineensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Melaniparus guineensis">Melaniparus guineensis</a></i></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Guinea" title="Economy of Guinea">Economy of Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2085" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional depiction of Guinea's export products</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea,_Africa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg/250px-Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg/375px-Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg/500px-Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2828" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea,_Africa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Malinke fisher women on the Niger River, <a href="/wiki/Niandankoro" title="Niandankoro">Niandankoro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kankan_Region" title="Kankan Region">Kankan Region</a>, in eastern Guinea</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kissidougou_market.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kissidougou_market.JPG/250px-Kissidougou_market.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kissidougou_market.JPG/375px-Kissidougou_market.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Kissidougou_market.JPG/500px-Kissidougou_market.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kissidougou_market.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kissidougou" title="Kissidougou">Kissidougou</a> market</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guinea has abundant natural resources including 25% or more of the world's known <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a> reserves. Guinea also has diamonds, gold, and other metals. The country has great potential for <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric power">hydroelectric power</a>. Bauxite and <a href="/wiki/Aluminium_oxide" title="Aluminium oxide">alumina</a> are currently the only major exports. Other industries include processing plants for beer, juices, soft drinks and tobacco. Agriculture employs 80% of the nation's labor force. Under French rule, and at the beginning of independence, Guinea was a major exporter of bananas, <a href="/wiki/Pineapples" class="mw-redirect" title="Pineapples">pineapples</a>, coffee, peanuts, and <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>. Guinea has considerable potential for growth in the agricultural and fishing sectors. Soil, water, and climatic conditions provide opportunities for large-scale irrigated farming and agro industry.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Guinea" title="Mining industry of Guinea">Mining industry of Guinea</a></div>
<p>Guinea possesses over 25&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a> (metric tons) of <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a> – and perhaps up to one-half of the world's reserves. In addition, Guinea's mineral wealth includes more than 4-billion tonnes of high-grade <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, significant diamond and gold deposits, and undetermined quantities of <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>. Possibilities for investment and commercial activities exist in all these areas, but Guinea's poorly developed <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> and rampant <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a> continue to present obstacles to large-scale investment projects.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">Joint venture</a> <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a> mining and alumina operations in northwest Guinea historically provide about 80% of Guinea's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_reserves" title="Foreign exchange reserves">foreign exchange</a>. Bauxite is refined into alumina, which is later <a href="/wiki/Smelting" title="Smelting">smelted</a> into aluminium.  The <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Compagnie_des_Bauxites_de_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Compagnie des Bauxites de Guinea (page does not exist)">Compagnie des Bauxites de Guinea</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compagnie_des_Bauxites_de_Guinea" class="extiw" title="fr:Compagnie des Bauxites de Guinea">fr</a>&#93;</span></i> (CBG), which exports about 14 million tonnes of high-grade bauxite annually, is the main player in the bauxite industry. CBG is a joint venture, 49% owned by the Guinean government and 51% by an international consortium known as <a href="/wiki/Halco_Mining" title="Halco Mining">Halco Mining</a> Inc., itself a joint venture controlled by aluminium producer <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a> (AA), global miner <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Tinto Group">Rio Tinto Group</a> and Dadco Investments.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> CBG has exclusive rights to bauxite reserves and resources in north-western Guinea through 2038.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In 2008 protesters upset about poor electrical services blocked the tracks CBG uses. Guineau often includes a proviso in its agreements with international oil companies requiring its partners to generate power for nearby communities.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Compagnie des Bauxites de Kindia</i> (CBK), a joint venture between the government of Guinea and <a href="/wiki/United_Company_RUSAL" class="mw-redirect" title="United Company RUSAL">RUSAL</a>, produces some 2.5&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a> annually, nearly all of which is exported to <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and Eastern Europe. <a href="/wiki/Dian_Dian" class="mw-redirect" title="Dian Dian">Dian Dian</a>, a Guinean/<a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> joint bauxite venture, has a projected production rate of 1,000,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">t</a> (1,102,311 <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">short tons</a>; 984,207 <a href="/wiki/Long_ton" title="Long ton">long tons</a>) per year, but is not expected to begin operation for several years. The <i><a href="/wiki/Alumina_Company_of_Guinea" title="Alumina Company of Guinea">Alumina Compagnie de Guinée</a></i> (ACG), which took over the former Friguia Consortium, produced about 2.4&#160;million tonnes in 2004 as raw material for its alumina refinery. The refinery exports about 750,000 tonnes of alumina. Both Global Alumina and Alcoa-Alcan have signed conventions with the government of Guinea to build large alumina refineries with a combined capacity of about 4 million tonnes per year.
</p><p>Diamonds and gold also are mined and exported on a large scale. The bulk of diamonds are mined <a href="/wiki/Artisanal_mining" title="Artisanal mining">artisanally</a>. The largest gold mining operation in Guinea is a joint venture between the government and <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Goldfields" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashanti Goldfields">Ashanti Goldfields</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>. AREDOR, a joint diamond-mining venture between the Guinean Government (50%) and an Australian, British, and Swiss <a href="/wiki/Consortium" title="Consortium">consortium</a>, began production in 1984 and mined diamonds that were 90% gem quality. Production stopped from 1993 until 1996, when First City Mining of Canada purchased the international portion of the consortium. Société Minière de Dinguiraye (SMD) also has a large gold mining facility in Lero, near the Malian border.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil">Oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guinea signed a <a href="/wiki/Production_sharing_agreement" title="Production sharing agreement">production sharing agreement</a> with Hyperdynamics Corporation of <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> in 2006 to explore a large offshore tract, and was recently in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Dana_Petroleum" title="Dana Petroleum">Dana Petroleum</a> PLC (<a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, United Kingdom). The initial well, the Sabu-1, was scheduled to begin drilling in October 2011 at a site in approximately 700&#160;meters of water.  The Sabu-1 targeted a four-way <a href="/wiki/Anticline" title="Anticline">anticline</a> prospect with <a href="/wiki/Upper_Cretaceous" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Cretaceous">upper Cretaceous</a> sands and was anticipated to be drilled to a total depth of 3,600&#160;meters.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Following the completion of exploratory <a href="/wiki/Drilling" title="Drilling">drilling</a> in 2012, the Sabu-1 well was not deemed commercially viable.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012, Hyperdynamics subsidiary SCS reached an agreement for a sale of 40% of the concession to <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a>, bringing ownership shares in the Guinea offshore tract to 37% Hyperdynamics, 40% Tullow Oil, and 23% Dana Petroleum.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Hyperdynamics will have until September 2016 under the current agreement to begin drilling its next selected site, the Fatala <a href="/wiki/Cenomanian" title="Cenomanian">Cenomanian</a> <a href="/wiki/Turbidite" title="Turbidite">turbidite</a> fan prospect.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></p><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x,
